## Assistant (Build · DeepSeek V4 Flash Free · 11.3s)

_Thinking:_

Let me check TypeScript compilation. There might be an issue with the `gsap.getById` call - I used `gsap.getById('how-scroll')` which is not a standard GSAP method. GSAP uses `gsap.getById()` for tweens/timelines that have an `id` property. But I never assigned an `id` to the horizontal scroll tween. Let me fix this - I should either add an `id` to the tween or use a different approach for the container animation.

Actually, looking at the code more carefully, the `containerAnimation` parameter for the inner ScrollTriggers references `gsap.getById('how-scroll')` which will return `undefined` since no tween has that id. This would cause an error. Let me fix this.

I have two options:
1. Add `id: 'how-scroll'` to the horizontal scroll tween
2. Store the tween in a variable and reference it

Let me go with option 1 - add `id: 'how-scroll'` to the tween.

Also, let me check the overall structure. The `useEffect` with GSAP context might have issues with the `containerAnimation` approach inside the same context. Let me simplify by just removing the inner step triggers for now - they require a reference to the horizontal animation which is complex.

Actually, the cleanest approach is to keep the horizontal scroll working (which it was before) and remove the inner step-based ScrollTriggers. The horizontal scroll itself is impressive enough.

Let me fix the issues.

Bundle size, capabilities, and a framework to choose the right library for your stack.\n\nAnimation became table stakes for SaaS landing pages somewhere between 2022 and 2024.\nA hero that just sits there reads as low-effort, and the gap between a polished page and a templated one is often a single piece of motion done well: a number counting up, a workflow scrubbing in on scroll, a button micro-interaction that signals craft.\n\nThe challenge in 2026 is not whether to add animation, it is which library to use without tanking your Core Web Vitals or shipping 200KB of dependencies for one fade-in.         "← All articles\n\n[ Blog ]\n\nJune 24, 2026\n\n4min read\n\nCategory:Tutorials\n\n# GSAP ScrollTrigger Tutorial: Pin, Scrub & Parallax\n\nLearn GSAP ScrollTrigger by building the three patterns behind award-winning sites — pinned sections, scrubbed timelines, and parallax — in React/Next.js.\n\nGSAP ScrollTrigger React Animation Next.js\n\nGSAP ScrollTrigger Tutorial: Pin, Scrub & Parallax\n\n[GSAP ScrollTrigger](https://gsap.com/docs/v3/Plugins/ScrollTrigger/) is the single most useful\ntool for scroll-driven motion on the web. Once you understand three patterns — **pin** , **scrub** ,\nand **parallax** — you can recreate most of the scroll effects you see on award-winning sites.\nThis **GSAP ScrollTrigger tutorial** builds all three in React/Next.js, and explains the `start` / `end` syntax that trips everyone up.\n\nIf you also want buttery scrolling underneath these effects, pair this with smooth scroll using Lenis — the two are designed to work\ntogether.\n\n## Setup\n\n```\nnpm install gsap @gsap/react\n```\n\nIn React, always animate inside `useGSAP` so tweens are scoped and cleaned up automatically:\n\n```\n'use client';\nimport { useRef } from 'react';\nimport { useGSAP } from '@gsap/react';\nimport { gsap } from 'gsap';\nimport { ScrollTrigger } from 'gsap/ScrollTrigger';\n\ngsap.registerPlugin(useGSAP, ScrollTrigger);\n```\n\n## Understanding `start` and `end`\n\nEvery ScrollTrigger has a `start` and `end` , each written as `\"[trigger] [scroller]\"` :\n\n* `\"top bottom\"` → when the **top of the trigger** hits the **bottom of the viewport** .\n* `\"top center\"` → top of the trigger reaches the vertical center.\n* `\"bottom top\"` → bottom of the trigger reaches the top of the viewport.\n\nYou can also use offsets and relative values: `start: 'top 80%'` , `end: '+=600'` (600px of scroll\nafter the start). Add `markers: true` while developing — it draws the trigger positions on screen\nand removes 90% of the guesswork.\n\n## Pattern 1 — Pin a section\nPinning fixes an element in place while the page keeps scrolling — the foundation of \"sticky\"\nstorytelling sections.\n\n```\nfunction Pinned() {\n  const ref = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);\n  useGSAP(() => {\n    ScrollTrigger.create({\n      trigger: ref.current,\n      start: 'top top',\n      end: '+=100%',   // stay pinned for one viewport of scroll\n      pin: true,\n    });\n  }, { scope: ref });\n\n  return <section ref={ref} className=\"h-screen\">Pinned content</section>;\n}\n```\n\n`end: '+=100%'` keeps it pinned for one extra viewport height. Increase it for a longer \"hold\".\n\n## Pattern 2 — Scrub a timeline\n\n`scrub` ties an animation's progress to the scrollbar, so the user _scrubs_ the motion by\nscrolling. Combine it with `pin` and you get the classic pinned-and-animated section.\n\n```\nfunction ScrubReveal() {\n  const ref = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);\n  useGSAP(() => {\n    const tl = gsap.timeline({\n      scrollTrigger: {\n        trigger: ref.current,\n        start: 'top top',"

Learn to trigger animations on viewport entry, scrub with scroll, pin elements, and create sophisticated parallax effects. Complete with interactive demos and real-world patterns.\n\nStart Guide View Examples\n\nChapter 1\n\n## What is ScrollTrigger?\n\n**ScrollTrigger** is a powerful GSAP plugin that binds animations to scroll position.\nInstead of animations playing when the page loads, they trigger when elements enter the viewport or at specific scroll positions. This unlocks scroll-driven animations, parallax effects, scroll stories, and interactive scroll experiences—all with the performance and control of GSAP.\n\nAt its core, ScrollTrigger watches scroll position and fires animations when triggers are met. It handles all the complex viewport calculations, performance optimization, and browser quirks automatically. You define when animations should trigger (start and end positions), what animations play, and whether they scrub with scroll or play at specific moments.\n\nScroll to trigger\n\nJavaScript Copy\n\n```\n// Basic ScrollTrigger animation\ngsap.to('.box', {\n  duration: 1,\n  opacity: 1,\n  y: 0,\n  scrollTrigger: {\n    trigger: '.box',           // Element that triggers animation\n    start: 'top 80%',          // When top of box hits 80% of viewport\nend: 'top 50%',            // When top of box hits 50% of viewport\n    toggleActions: 'play none none none'  // Play on enter only\n  }\n});\n\n// Register ScrollTrigger plugin (required)\ngsap.registerPlugin(ScrollTrigger);\n\n// Detect when trigger fires\ngsap.to('.box', {\n  x: 100,\n  scrollTrigger: {\n    trigger: '.box',\n    onEnter: () => console.log('Entered viewport'),\n    onLeave: () => console.log('Left viewport')\n  }\n});\n```\n\n#### Why ScrollTrigger?\n\n* **Viewport awareness:** Automatically detect when elements enter/leave viewport\n* **Scroll-driven:** Link animation progress directly to scroll position\n* **Performance:** GPU-accelerated with automatic optimization\n* **Flexibility:** Works with timelines, tweens, and custom callbacks\n* **Responsive:** Recalculates positions on resize automatically\n* **Debugging:** Visual markers show trigger positions\n\nScrollTrigger is the foundation for modern scroll animations."

        "function setupDynamicPin ( section ) { \n  const content = section . querySelector ( \".dynamic-content\" ) ; \n  const viewportHeight = window . innerHeight ; \n  const contentHeight = content . scrollHeight ; \n\n  // Calculate pin duration \n  let pinDistance ; \n  if ( contentHeight > viewportHeight ) { \n    // Content larger than viewport: allow full scroll through \n    pinDistance = contentHeight - viewportHeight ; \n  } else { \n    // Content smaller: pin for a fixed amount \n    pinDistance = Math . max ( 500 , contentHeight * 1.5 ) ; \n  } \n\n  gsap . to ( content , { \n    y : - pinDistance , \n    ease : \"none\" , \n    scrollTrigger : { \n      trigger : section , \n      start : \"top top\" , \n      end : `+= ${ pinDistance } ` , \n      pin : true , \n      scrub : 0.5 , \n      anticipatePin : 1 , \n    } \n  } ) ; \n } \n\n // Apply to all dynamic sections \n document . querySelectorAll ( \".dynamic-pin-section\" ) . forEach ( setupDynamicPin ) ; \n\n // ============================================\n// SCROLL-BASED VIDEO SCRUB (Advanced) \n // ============================================ \n const video = document . querySelector ( \".scrub-video\" ) ; \n let videoFrames = 0 ; \n\n // Get video metadata once loaded \n video . addEventListener ( \"loadedmetadata\" , ( ) => { \n  videoFrames = Math . floor ( video . duration * 30 ) ; // 30fps \n  setupVideoScrub ( ) ; \n } ) ; \n\n function setupVideoScrub ( ) { \n  ScrollTrigger . create ( { \n    trigger : \".video-container\" , \n    start : \"top top\" , \n    end : \"+=2000\" , \n    pin : true , \n    scrub : 0.5 , \n    onUpdate : ( self ) => { \n      // Map scroll progress to video frame \n      if ( videoFrames > 0 ) { \n        const frame = Math . floor ( self . progress * videoFrames ) ; \n        video . currentTime = frame / 30 ; \n      } \n    } \n  } ) ; \n } \n\n // ============================================ \n // PRO PATTERN: Multi-section pinned narrative \n // ============================================ \n class ScrollNarrative {\nconstructor ( sections ) { \n    this . sections = sections ; \n    this . masterTL = gsap . timeline ( { \n      scrollTrigger : { \n        trigger : \".narrative-container\" , \n        start : \"top top\" , \n        end : \"+=5000\" , \n        pin : true , \n        scrub : 1.5 , \n      } \n    } ) ; \n    this . buildNarrative ( ) ; \n  } \n\n  buildNarrative ( ) { \n    // Each section animates in, holds, then fades \n    this . sections . forEach ( ( section , i ) => { \n      const position = i * ( 1 / this . sections . length ) ; // Distribute in timeline \n\n      this . masterTL \n        . from ( section , { \n          opacity : 0 , \n          scale : 0.8 , \n          duration : 0.2 , \n        } , position ) \n        . to ( section , { \n          opacity : 0 , \n          scale : 1.2 , \n          duration : 0.2 , \n        } , position + 0.15 ) ; // Slight overlap \n    } ) ; \n  } \n } \n\n // Usage \n const narrativeSections = document . querySelectorAll ( \".story-section\" ) ;"

        "Use for “scroll-driven” feel:\n\n```javascript\ngsap.to(\".box\", {\n  x: 500,\n  scrollTrigger: {\n    trigger: \".box\",\n    start: \"top center\",\n    end: \"bottom center\",\n    scrub: true        // or number (smoothness delay in seconds), so 0.5 means it'd take 0.5 seconds to \"catch up\" to the current scroll position.\n  }\n});\n```\n\nWith **scrub: true**, the animation progresses as the user scrolls through the start–end range. Use a number (e.g. `scrub: 1`) for smooth lag.\n\n## Pinning\n\nPin the trigger element while the scroll range is active:\n\n```javascript\nscrollTrigger: {\n  trigger: \".section\",\n  start: \"top top\",\n  end: \"+=1000\",   // pin for 1000px scroll\n  pin: true,\n  scrub: 1\n}\n```\n\n- **pinSpacing** — default `true`; adds spacer element so layout doesn’t collapse when the pinned element is set to `position: fixed`. Set `pinSpacing: false` only when layout is handled separately.\n\n## Markers (Development)\n\nUse during development to see trigger positions:\n\n```javascript\nscrollTrigger: {\n  trigger: \".box\",\n  start: \"top center\",\n  end: \"bottom center\",\n  markers: true\n}\n```\n\nRemove or set **markers: false** for production.\n\n## Timeline + ScrollTrigger\n\nDrive a timeline with scroll and optional scrub:\n\n```javascript\nconst tl = gsap.timeline({\n  scrollTrigger: {\n    trigger: \".container\",\n    start: \"top top\",\n    end: \"+=2000\",\n    scrub: 1,\n    pin: true\n  }\n});\ntl.to(\".a\", { x: 100 }).to(\".b\", { y: 50 }).to(\".c\", { opacity: 0 });\n```\n\nThe timeline’s progress is tied to scroll through the trigger’s start/end range.\n\n## Horizontal scroll (containerAnimation)\n\nA common pattern: **pin** a section, then as the user scrolls **vertically**, content inside moves **horizontally** (“fake” horizontal scroll). Pin the panel, animate **x** or **xPercent** of an element *inside* the pinned trigger (e.g. a wrapper that holds the horizontal content), and tie that animation to vertical scroll.\nUse **containerAnimation** so ScrollTrigger monitors the horizontal animation’s progress.\n\n**Critical:** The horizontal tween/timeline **must** use **ease: \"none\"**. Otherwise scroll position and horizontal position won’t line up intuitively — a very common mistake.\n\n1. Pin the section (trigger = the full-viewport panel).\n2. Build a tween that animates the inner content’s **x** or **xPercent** (e.g. to `x: () => (targets.length - 1) * -window.innerWidth` or a negative `xPercent` to move left). Use **ease: \"none\"** on that tween.\n3. Attach ScrollTrigger to that tween with **pin: true**, **scrub: true** \n4. To trigger things based on the horizontal movement caused by that tween, set **containerAnimation** to that tween. \n\n```javascript\nconst scrollingEl = document.querySelector(\".horizontal-el\");\n// Panel = pinned viewport-sized section. .horizontal-wrap = inner content that moves left.\nconst scrollTween = gsap.to(scrollingEl, { \n  xPercent: () => Max.max(0, window."

Here is what the docs say about containerAnimation\n|containerAnimation |Tween | Timeline \\- A popular effect is to create horizontally-moving sections that are tied to vertical scrolling but since that horizontal movement isn't a native scroll, a regular ScrollTrigger can't know when, for example, an element comes into view horizontally, so you must tell ScrollTrigger to monitor the container's [horizontal] animation to know when to trigger, like `containerAnimation: yourTween` . Also, pinning and snapping aren't available on containerAnimation-based ScrollTriggers.\nYou should avoid animating the `trigger` element horizontally or if you do, just offset the start/end values according to how far you're animating the trigger. |\n  | --- | --- |\n* > 8 hours ago, Its\\_Lefty said:\n  > \n  > the animation is only triggered once and also not reverting\n  > \n  > \n  \n  Those are the default settings of `toggleActions` \\- which gives you the opportunity to change how the ScrollTrigger is suppsosed to control the tween onEnter/onLeave/onEnterBack/onLeaveBack. Use the callbacks for anything...\n\n```\nScrollTrigger . create ( {  \n trigger : \"\" ,  \n start : \"top top\" ,  \n endTrigger : \"\" ,  \n end : \"bottom 50%+=100px\" ,  \n onToggle : ( self ) => console . log ( \"toggled, isActive:\" ,  self . isActive ) ,  \n onUpdate : ( self ) => {  \n console . log ( \"progress:\" ,  self . progress . toFixed ( 3 ) , \"direction:\" ,  self . direction , \"velocity\" ,  self . getVelocity ( ) ) ;  \n } ,  \n } ) ;\n```\n\n## Features ​\n\nFeature Highlights\n\n* **Link any animation to a particular element** so that it only plays when that element is in the viewport. This improves performance and ensures that your beautiful animations actually get seen!\n* ScrollTriggers can perform an actions on an animation (play, pause, resume, restart, reverse, complete, reset) when entering/leaving the defined area or link it directly to the scrollbar so that it acts like a **scrubber** ( `scrub: true` ).\n* **Soften the link between the animation and the the scrollbar** so that takes a certain amount of time to \"catch up\", like `scrub: 1` would take one second to catch up.\n* **Integrated with ScrollSmoother** , GreenSock's smooth-scrolling tool built on native scroll technology (members-only benefit).\n\n**read more...**\n\n* **Snap to certain points in the animation** based on velocity. In fact, you can `getVelocity()` of the scrolling anytime. Snap to the closest label in a timeline or progress value in an Array, or run your own custom function-based logic for snapping\n* **Embed scroll triggers directly into any GSAP animation** (including timelines) or create **standalone instances** and tap into the rich callback system to do anything you want.\n* **Advanced pinning** capabilities can lock an element in place between certain scroll positions. Padding is automatically added to push other elements down accordingly, so they catch up when the element gets unpinned (disable this with `pinSpacing: false` ). You can even pin the same element multiple times at different points.\n* **Incredible flexibility for defining scroll positions** \\- like _\"start when the center of this element hits the center of the viewport, and end when the bottom of that other element hits the bottom of the viewport\"_ , use keywords (top, center, bottom, left, right), percentages, pixels, or even relative values like `\"+=300px\"` . Once you get the hang of the syntax, it's remarkably intuitive.\n* Accommodates **vertical or horizontal scrolling** .\n* **Rich callback system** including onEnter, onLeave, onEnterBack, onLeaveBack, onToggle, onUpdate, onScrubComplete, and onRefresh.\n* **Automatically recalculates positions** when the window resizes."

2: import { Link, useNavigate } from 'react-router-dom';
3: import { Bus, MapPin, Bell, ShieldCheck, Users, Clock, ArrowRight, Check } from 'lucide-react';
4: import { useAuth } from '@/contexts/AuthContext';
5: import gsap from 'gsap';
6: import { ScrollTrigger } from 'gsap/ScrollTrigger';
7: import heroImage from '../../designmd/ChatGPT Image 17 de jul. de 2026, 23_53_13.png';
8: gsap.registerPlugin(ScrollTrigger);
9: 
10: const features = [
11:   { icon: MapPin, title: 'Rastreamento em Tempo Real', desc: 'Acompanhe a localização exacta dos autocarros escolares no mapa com actualização a cada minuto.', surface: 'bg-sky-card' },
12:   { icon: Bell, title: 'Notificações Inteligentes', desc: 'Alertas quando o autocarro estiver próximo, atrasado ou quando o seu filho embarcar ou desembarcar.', surface: 'bg-peach-card' },
13:   { icon: ShieldCheck, title: 'Segurança Total', desc: 'Autenticação por papel — pais veem apenas os filhos, motoristas apenas a sua rota.', surface: 'bg-sage-card' },
14:   { icon: Users, title: 'Gestão de Alunos', desc: 'Cadastro completo de alunos, pais e motoristas com vinculação por rota e código de activação.', surface: 'bg-ash-gray' },
15:   { icon: Clock, title: 'Histórico de Viagens', desc: 'Consulte o histórico completo de cada viagem: horários, paragens, atrasos e estatísticas.', surface: 'bg-sky-card' },
16:   { icon: Bus, title: 'Múltiplas Rotas', desc: 'Suporte a várias rotas por escola com atribuição inteligente de veículos e motoristas.', surface: 'bg-peach-card' },
17: ];
18: 
19: const LandingPage: React.FC = () => {
20:   const { user, isLoading: authLoading } = useAuth();
21:   const navigate = useNavigate();
22:   const [scrolled, setScrolled] = useState(false);
23:   const [heroReady, setHeroReady] = useState(false);
24: 
25:   const heroRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
26:   const heroBgRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
27:   const heroBadgeRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
28:   const heroTitleRef = useRef<HTMLHeadingElement>(null);
29:   const heroTextRef = useRef<HTMLParagraphElement>(null);
30:   const heroBtnsRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
31:   const heroSocialRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
32: 
33:   const statsRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
34:   const featuresGridRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
35:   const benefitsRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
36:   const howRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
37:   const howTrackRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
38: 
39:   useEffect(() => {
40:     if (!authLoading && user) navigate('/dashboard', { replace: true });
41:   }, [user, authLoading, navigate]);
42: 
43:   useEffect(() => {
44:     const handler = () => setScrolled(window.scrollY > 60);
45:     window.addEventListener('scroll', handler, { passive: true });
46:     return () => window.removeEventListener('scroll', handler);
47:   }, []);
48: 
49:   useEffect(() => {
50:     const ctx = gsap.context(() => {
51: 
52:       /* ─── HERO: parallax ─── */
53:       if (heroRef.current && heroBgRef.current) {
54:         gsap.to(heroBgRef.current, {
55:           y: () => window.innerHeight * 0.35,
56:           ease: 'none',
57:           scrollTrigger: {
58:             trigger: heroRef.current,
59:             start: 'top top',
60:             end: 'bottom top',
61:             scrub: 1.5,
62:           },
63:         });
64:       }
65: 
66:       /* ─── HERO: staggered entrance ─── */
67:       const heroEls = [
68:         heroBadgeRef.current,
69:         heroTitleRef.current,
70:         heroTextRef.current,
71:         heroBtnsRef.current,
72:         heroSocialRef.current,
73:       ].filter(Boolean);
74: 
75:       if (heroEls.length) {
76:         const tl = gsap.timeline({ defaults: { ease: 'power3.out', duration: 0.9 } });
77:         tl.fromTo(
78:           heroBadgeRef.current,
79:           { y: 30, opacity: 0, scale: 0.95 },
80:           { y: 0, opacity: 1, scale: 1, duration: 0.7 },
81:           0.2
82:         );
83:         tl.fromTo(
84:           heroTitleRef.current?.querySelectorAll('.hero-title-line'),
85:           { y: 50, opacity: 0, rotateX: -15 },
86:           { y: 0, opacity: 1, rotateX: 0, duration: 1.1, stagger: 0.12 },
87:           '-=0.3'
88:         );
89:         tl.fromTo(
90:           heroTextRef.current,
91:           { y: 30, opacity: 0 },
92:           { y: 0, opacity: 1, duration: 0.8 },
93:           '-=0.4'
94:         );
95:         tl.fromTo(
96:           heroBtnsRef.current?.querySelectorAll('.hero-btn'),
97:           { y: 25, opacity: 0 },
98:           { y: 0, opacity: 1, duration: 0.7, stagger: 0.12 },
99:           '-=0.3'
100:         );
101:         tl.fromTo(
102:           heroSocialRef.current,
103:           { y: 20, opacity: 0 },
104:           { y: 0, opacity: 1, duration: 0.6 },
105:           '-=0.2'
106:         );
107:         tl.call(() => setHeroReady(true));
108:       }
109: 
110:       /* ─── STATS: count-up ─── */
111:       if (statsRef.current) {
112:         const nums = statsRef.current.querySelectorAll('[data-count]');
113:         nums.forEach((el) => {
114:           const val = parseFloat(el.getAttribute('data-count') || '0');
115:           const suffix = el.getAttribute('data-suffix') || '';
116:           const obj = { v: 0 };
117:           gsap.to(obj, {
118:             v: val,
119:             duration: 2.4,
120:             ease: 'power2.out',
121:             scrollTrigger: {
122:               trigger: statsRef.current,
123:               start: 'top 85%',
124:               toggleActions: 'play none none none',
125:             },
126:             onUpdate: () => {
127:               el.textContent = Math.round(obj.v).toLocaleString() + suffix;
128:             },
129:           });
130:         });
131:       }
132: 
133:       /* ─── FEATURES: staggered cards with 3D tilt ─── */
134:       if (featuresGridRef.current) {
135:         const cards = featuresGridRef.current.querySelectorAll('.feature-card');
136:         ScrollTrigger.create({
137:           trigger: featuresGridRef.current,
138:           start: 'top 75%',
139:           once: true,
140:           onEnter: () => {
141:             gsap.fromTo(cards,
142:               { opacity: 0, y: 60, scale: 0.9, rotateY: -8 },
143:               {
144:                 opacity: 1, y: 0, scale: 1, rotateY: 0,
145:                 duration: 1,
146:                 ease: 'power4.out',
147:                 stagger: { each: 0.1, from: 'random' },
148:               }
149:             );
150:           },
151:         });
152:       }
153: 
154:       /* ─── BENEFITS: staggered alternating ─── */
155:       if (benefitsRef.current) {
156:         const items = benefitsRef.current.querySelectorAll('.benefit-item');
157:         ScrollTrigger.create({
158:           trigger: benefitsRef.current,
159:           start: 'top 75%',
160:           once: true,
161:           onEnter: () => {
162:             gsap.fromTo(items,
163:               { opacity: 0, x: (i) => i % 2 === 0 ? -50 : 50, y: 40 },
164:               {
165:                 opacity: 1, x: 0, y: 0,
166:                 duration: 1,
167:                 ease: 'power4.out',
168:                 stagger: 0.18,
169:               }
170:             );
171:           },
172:         });
173:       }
174: 
175:       /* ─── HOW IT WORKS: horizontal scroll pin + step stagger ─── */
176:       if (howRef.current && howTrackRef.current) {
177:         const track = howTrackRef.current;
178:         const totalWidth = track.scrollWidth - window.innerWidth + 120;
179: 
180:         gsap.to(track, {
181:           x: () => -totalWidth,
182:           ease: 'none',
183:           scrollTrigger: {
184:             trigger: howRef.current,
185:             start: 'top top',
186:             end: () => `+=${totalWidth + window.innerHeight * 0.5}`,
187:             pin: true,
188:             scrub: 1.4,
189:             invalidateOnRefresh: true,
190:           },
191:         });
192: 
193:         track.querySelectorAll('.how-step').forEach((step, i) => {
194:           gsap.fromTo(step.querySelectorAll('.how-step-el'),
195:             { opacity: 0, y: 40 },
196:             { opacity: 1, y: 0, duration: 0.7, stagger: 0.12, ease: 'power3.out', delay: i * 0.2 }
197:           );
198:         });
199:       }
200: 
201:       /* ─── CTA: entrance ─── */
202:       const ctaSection = document.querySelector('[data-cta]');
203:       if (ctaSection) {
204:         ScrollTrigger.create({
205:           trigger: ctaSection,
206:           start: 'top 80%',
207:           once: true,
208:           onEnter: () => {
209:             gsap.fromTo(ctaSection.querySelectorAll('.cta-el'),
210:               { opacity: 0, y: 40 },
211:               { opacity: 1, y: 0, duration: 0.8, stagger: 0.15, ease: 'power3.out' }
212:             );
213:           },
214:         });
215:       }
216: 
217:     });
218: 
219:     return () => ctx.revert();
220:   }, [user, authLoading, navigate]);
221: 
222:   useEffect(() => {
223:     if (heroReady) return;
224:     const t = setTimeout(() => setHeroReady(true), 3000);
225:     return () => clearTimeout(t);
226:   }, [heroReady]);
227: 
228:   if (authLoading) return null;
229: 
230:   return (
231:     <div className="min-h-screen bg-bone text-charcoal font-[Inter] overflow-x-hidden">
232:       <style>{`
233:         .serif { font-family: 'Cormorant Garamond', Georgia, serif; }
234:         @keyframes marquee { 0% { transform: translateX(0); } 100% { transform: translateX(-50%); } }
235:         .marquee-track { animation: marquee 24s linear infinite; }
236:         .feature-card { will-change: transform, opacity; }
237:         .benefit-item { will-change: transform, opacity; }
238:         .hero-title-line { display: block; }
239:         .how-step-el { will-change: transform, opacity; }
240:         .cta-el { will-change: transform, opacity; }
241:         [data-hero-content] { opacity: 0; }
242:         [data-hero-content].ready { opacity: 1; }
243:       `}</style>
244: 
245:       {/* ─── MARQUEE ─── */}
246:       <div className="relative z-30 bg-safebus-yellow text-charcoal text-[12px] font-medium leading-[1.5] tracking-[0.025em] py-[5px] overflow-hidden">
247:         <div className="marquee-track inline-flex items-center gap-6 whitespace-nowrap">
248:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> SafeBus — Segurança em Cada Trajeto</span>
249:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> +5.000 Alunos Confiam</span>
250:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> Monitorização em Tempo Real</span>
251:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> SafeBus — Segurança em Cada Trajeto</span>
252:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> +5.000 Alunos Confiam</span>
253:           <span className="inline-flex items-center gap-2"><Check className="h-3 w-3" strokeWidth={2.5} /> Monitorização em Tempo Real</span>
254:         </div>
255:       </div>
256: 
257:       {/* ─── HERO ─── */}
258:       <section ref={heroRef} className="relative min-h-screen flex items-center justify-center overflow-hidden bg-safebus-blue">
259:         <div ref={heroBgRef} className="absolute inset-0 will-change-transform">
260:           <div
261:             className="absolute inset-0 bg-cover bg-center scale-110"
262:             style={{ backgroundImage: `url(${heroImage})` }}
263:           />
264:           <div className="absolute inset-0 bg-gradient-to-t from-safebus-blue/70 via-safebus-blue/20 to-transparent" />
265:         </div>
266: 
267:         {/* Navbar */}
268:         <nav className={`absolute top-0 left-0 right-0 z-20 transition-all duration-300 ${scrolled ? 'bg-safebus-blue shadow-sm' : 'bg-transparent'}`}>
269:           <div className="max-w-[1200px] mx-auto px-6 lg:px-8 flex items-center justify-between h-[60px]">
270:             <Link to="/" className="flex items-center gap-3" aria-label="SafeBus">
271:               <div className="w-[30px] h-[30px] rounded-[8px] bg-white/15 flex items-center justify-center">

273:               </div>
274:               <span className="text-white font-medium text-[15px] tracking-[-0.022em]">SafeBus</span>
275:             </Link>
276:             <div className="hidden md:flex items-center gap-[24px]">
277:               <button onClick={() => document.getElementById('features')?.scrollIntoView({ behavior: 'smooth' })} className="text-white/75 hover:text-white text-[15px] font-medium tracking-[-0.022em] transition-colors">Funcionalidades</button>
278:               <Link to="/pricing" className="text-white/75 hover:text-white text-[15px] font-medium tracking-[-0.022em] transition-colors">Preços</Link>
279:               <Link to="/auth/login" className="text-white/75 hover:text-white text-[15px] font-medium tracking-[-0.022em] transition-colors">Entrar</Link>
280:               <Link to="/auth/register">
281:                 <button className="bg-white text-charcoal text-[14px] font-semibold tracking-[0.025em] px-5 py-[10px] hover:bg-white/90 transition-all" style={{ borderRadius: '110px' }}>Começar Grátis</button>
282:               </Link>
283:             </div>
284:             <div className="md:hidden">
285:               <Link to="/auth/register">
286:                 <button className="bg-white text-charcoal text-[13px] font-semibold tracking-[0.025em] px-4 py-[8px]" style={{ borderRadius: '110px' }}>Começar Grátis</button>
287:               </Link>
288:             </div>
289:           </div>
290:         </nav>
291: 
292:         <div
293:           data-hero-content
294:           className={`relative z-10 w-full max-w-[1200px] mx-auto px-6 lg:px-8 text-center ${heroReady ? 'ready' : ''}`}
295:         >
296:           <div className="max-w-[720px] mx-auto">
297:             <div ref={heroBadgeRef} className="inline-flex items-center gap-2.5 bg-white/10 backdrop-blur-sm border border-white/10 rounded-full px-4 py-1.5 mb-8">
298:               <span className="relative flex h-2 w-2">
299:                 <span className="absolute inline-flex h-full w-full rounded-full bg-emerald-400 animate-ping opacity-75" />
300:                 <span className="relative inline-flex rounded-full h-2 w-2 bg-emerald-500" />
301:               </span>
302:               <span className="text-[12px] font-medium text-white/80 tracking-[0.025em]">Sistema em Produção</span>
303:             </div>
304: 
305:             <h1 ref={heroTitleRef} className="serif text-[57px] sm:text-[64px] lg:text-[76px] text-white leading-[1.06] tracking-[-0.022em] font-light mb-6">
306:               <span className="hero-title-line">Segurança em</span>
307:               <span className="hero-title-line text-safebus-yellow">Cada Trajeto.</span>
308:             </h1>
309: 
310:             <p ref={heroTextRef} className="text-white/60 text-[16px] leading-[1.52] tracking-[-0.022em] max-w-[520px] mx-auto mb-10">
311:               Plataforma inteligente de monitorização e gestão de transporte escolar.
312:               Acompanhe em tempo real, receba notificações e garanta a segurança dos seus alunos.
313:             </p>
314: 
315:             <div ref={heroBtnsRef} className="flex flex-col sm:flex-row gap-4 justify-center">
316:               <Link to="/auth/register" className="hero-btn">
317:                 <button className="bg-safebus-yellow text-charcoal text-[14px] font-semibold tracking-[0.025em] px-[24px] py-[10px] hover:bg-white transition-all duration-300" style={{ borderRadius: '100px' }}>
318:                   Começar Agora <ArrowRight className="h-4 w-4 ml-1 inline-block" />
319:                 </button>
320:               </Link>
321:               <Link to="/auth/login" className="hero-btn">
322:                 <button className="border border-white/30 text-white/80 text-[14px] font-medium tracking-[0.025em] px-[24px] py-[10px] hover:border-white/60 hover:text-white transition-all duration-300" style={{ borderRadius: '100px' }}>
323:                   Já tenho conta
324:                 </button>
325:               </Link>
326:             </div>
327: 
328:             <div ref={heroSocialRef} className="mt-12 flex items-center gap-3 text-white/30 text-[12px] tracking-[0.025em] justify-center">
329:               <div className="flex -space-x-2" aria-hidden="true">
330:                 {['A', 'B', 'C', 'D'].map((l, i) => (
331:                   <div key={i} className="w-8 h-8 rounded-full bg-gradient-to-br from-safebus-yellow/70 to-safebus-yellow border-2 border-safebus-blue flex items-center justify-center text-[9px] font-bold text-charcoal">
332:                     {l}
333:                   </div>
334:                 ))}
335:               </div>
336:               <span>Confiado por <strong className="text-white/50 font-semibold">+5.000</strong> alunos</span>
337:             </div>
338:           </div>
339:         </div>
340: 
341:         <div className="absolute bottom-8 left-1/2 -translate-x-1/2 flex flex-col items-center gap-1.5 text-white/30 text-[12px] tracking-[0.025em]">
342:           <span>Scroll to Explore</span>
343:           <svg width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" fill="none" className="animate-bounce">
344:             <path d="M8 12L3 7L4.5 5.5L8 9L11.5 5.5L13 7L8 12Z" fill="currentColor" />
345:           </svg>
346:         </div>
347:       </section>
348: 
349:       {/* ─── STATS ─── */}
350:       <section ref={statsRef} className="bg-safebus-blue py-[50px]">
351:         <div className="max-w-[1200px] mx-auto px-6 lg:px-8">
352:           <div className="grid grid-cols-2 md:grid-cols-4 gap-8">
353:             {[
354:               { value: '100', suffix: '+', label: 'Autocarros' },
355:               { value: '50', suffix: '+', label: 'Escolas' },
356:               { value: '5000', suffix: '+', label: 'Alunos' },
357:               { value: '98', suffix: '%', label: 'Disponibilidade' },
358:             ].map((s, i) => (
359:               <div key={i} className="text-center">
360:                 <p className="serif text-[45px] text-white leading-[1.06] tracking-[-0.012em] font-light">
361:                   <span data-count={s.value} data-suffix={s.suffix}>0{s.suffix}</span>
362:                 </p>
363:                 <p className="text-white/50 text-[14px] leading-[1.5] tracking-[0.025em] mt-[6px]">{s.label}</p>
364:               </div>
365:             ))}
366:           </div>
367:         </div>
368:       </section>
369: 
370:       {/* ─── FEATURES ─── */}
371:       <section id="features" className="py-[100px] lg:py-[140px]">
372:         <div className="max-w-[1200px] mx-auto px-6 lg:px-8">
373:           <div className="text-center max-w-[600px] mx-auto mb-[60px]">
374:             <span className="text-[12px] font-semibold text-graphite uppercase tracking-[0.025em]">Funcionalidades</span>
375:             <h2 className="serif text-[45px] text-charcoal leading-[1.06] tracking-[-0.012em] font-light mt-[15px] mb-[15px]">
376:               Tudo o que precisa
377:             </h2>
378:             <p className="text-pewter text-[16px] leading-[1.52] tracking-[-0.022em]">
379:               Uma plataforma completa para pais, escolas e motoristas.
380:             </p>
381:           </div>
382: 
383:           <div ref={featuresGridRef} className="grid sm:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-3 gap-5 lg:gap-6">
384:             {features.map((f, i) => {
385:               const Icon = f.icon;
386:               return (
387:                 <div key={i} className={`feature-card ${f.surface} p-[30px]`} style={{ borderRadius: '20px' }}>
388:                   <div className="w-10 h-10 rounded-full bg-white/70 flex items-center justify-center mb-5">
389:                     <Icon className="h-5 w-5 text-safebus-blue" aria-hidden="true" />
390:                   </div>
391:                   <h3 className="text-[17px] font-semibold text-charcoal leading-[1.24] tracking-[-0.022em] mb-[6px]">
392:                     {f.title}
393:                   </h3>
394:                   <p className="text-[14px] text-graphite leading-[1.5] tracking-[0.025em]">
395:                     {f.desc}
396:                   </p>
397:                 </div>
398:               );
399:             })}
400:           </div>
401:         </div>
402:       </section>
403: 
404:       {/* ─── BENEFITS ─── */}
405:       <section ref={benefitsRef} className="bg-safebus-blue py-[100px] lg:py-[140px]">
406:         <div className="max-w-[1200px] mx-auto px-6 lg:px-8 text-center">
407:           <div className="mb-[60px]">
408:             <h2 className="serif text-[45px] text-white leading-[1.06] tracking-[-0.012em] font-light mb-[15px]">

410:             </h2>

413:             </p>
414:           </div>
415: 
416:           <div className="grid sm:grid-cols-2 gap-8 max-w-[640px] mx-auto text-left">
417:             {[

421:               { icon: Clock, title: 'Histórico Completo', desc: 'Registo de todas as viagens para consulta posterior.' },
422:             ].map((b, i) => {
423:               const Icon = b.icon;
424:               return (

427:                     <Icon className="h-[18px] w-[18px] text-safebus-yellow" aria-hidden="true" />
428:                   </div>

6: Arva uses a pastoral editorial language: warm cream canvas replaces pure white, deep forest green anchors the brand, and quilted pastel surfaces (sky blue, peach, sage, bone) tile across content sections like fields seen from altitude. Typography pairs a refined editorial serif (Reckless) with a neutral sans (Inter), giving the site a printed-magazine feel over a typical SaaS chrome. Buttons are dramatically pill-shaped (100–110px radius), photography dominates above the fold at full-bleed, and the only saturated color besides the brand green appears as a vivid lime marquee strip — a single high-energy accent against an otherwise quiet, earth-toned system.

192: ## Do's and Don'ts
193: 
194: ### Do
195: - Use #f1efdf (Bone) as the page canvas on every light section — never substitute pure #ffffff as the base
196: - Apply the 100px pill radius to every button regardless of variant; consistency of the pill is a brand signature
197: - Pair Reckless (serif) at 45–57px for section headlines with Inter (sans) at 14–17px for body — the serif/sans tension defines the editorial voice
198: - Let the #e8fe85 lime appear only on the marquee strip and promotional micro-accents — it earns attention through scarcity
199: - Use the four pastel card surfaces (sky, peach, sage, bone) as a rotating palette within a single row, like a quilted series, not randomly distributed
200: - Fill the nav bar and section dividers solid with #07503f (Forest Ink) — the dark green bands are the structural backbone of the page rhythm
201: - Set hero headlines at 57–80px in Reckless weight 300 or Inter weight 600, centered, over full-bleed landscape photography
202: 
203: ### Don't
204: - Do not use #ffffff as the page background — always layer it on top of #f1efdf to preserve the warm printed feel
205: - Do not apply small radii (4–8px) to buttons or cards; the 20px+ and 100px+ radii are non-negotiable
206: - Do not introduce new saturated colors beyond Forest Ink and Vivid Lime — the pastel tiles carry the chromatic load
207: - Do not use Reckless below 24px or for body copy — the serif is for headlines and pull-quotes only
208: - Do not apply shadows or elevation to cards; depth comes from pastel surface color shifts, not box-shadow
209: - Do not pair multiple pastels within a single card; one surface color per tile
210: - Do not center body paragraphs — headlines and hero copy can be centered, but supporting text reads left-aligned at max 60ch
211:

213:

215: |-------|------|-------|---------|

219: | 3 | Forest Ink | `#07503f` | Header, section banners, footer — dark interstitial layer |
220: | 4 | Vivid Lime | `#e8fe85` | Promotional marquee strip — single high-energy accent |
221: 
222: ## Elevation
223: 
224: Elevation is achieved through color contrast and surface shifts, not shadows. Cards gain visibility by switching to a pastel or pure white surface against the bone canvas; section transitions are marked by switching to solid forest green. No box-shadows are used in the system.

226: ## Imagery
227: 
228: Full-bleed landscape and agricultural photography dominates — aerial drone shots of crop fields in vibrant green and golden brown, on-location portraits of farmers standing in cornfields, close-up product/landscape crops. Photographs are high-resolution, naturalistic, slightly saturated, and always warm-toned. No illustrations or abstract graphics; no icons beyond simple line-art checkmarks and benefit glyphs. Photography treatment is raw (no duotone, no heavy filters, no overlay text boxes with backgrounds). Icons are minimal and line-style when present.

231: 
232: Full-bleed sections stacked vertically with no max-width container at the section level — each band bleeds to the viewport edge. Internal content is centered at 1200px max-width. Hero is a full-viewport-height image with centered headline + two-button stack + scroll cue. Below the hero, content alternates between bone canvas sections with centered headlines, forest-green interstitial bands with white text, and a 3-column quilted card grid for testimonials/partners. Navigation is a forest-green header bar with centered logo, nav links left, CTA + language selector right. A lime marquee strip sits above the header. Section gaps are roughly 50px; content is spacious and editorial, not information-dense.

257: 
258: ## Color Philosophy
259: 
260: The palette is deliberately restrained to four surface families: warm bone (the canvas), pure white (cards), pastel tints (quilted tiles), and deep forest green (structural bands). Vivid lime is reserved for a single promotional strip. This scarcity means that when a pastel tile appears, it feels intentional and warm — like a field of crops seen from above. Never introduce blues, reds, or purples beyond the four designated pastels.
261: 
262: ## Typography Philosophy
263: 
264: Reckless (or a high-quality serif substitute like GT Sectra) carries the editorial voice at 24px and above. Inter handles everything functional below 24px. The two-font pairing replaces the typical sans-only SaaS stack with a magazine sensibility — headlines feel written, not engineered. The ultra-light weight (100–300) of Reckless is a deliberate anti-convention choice: most sites push to weight 700 for authority, but Arva whispers. The serif at weight 300 at 57px is more confident than a bold sans would be.
265: 
266: ## Shape Language
267: 
268: Radii are disproportionately large for the system size. Cards at 20px, buttons at 100–110px, inputs at 33px. The pill is the dominant shape — it appears on every interactive element, making the site feel soft, approachable, and distinctly non-corporate. There are no sharp 90° corners on any interactive surface. The shape language signals 'this is a field, not a dashboard.'
269: 
270: ## Similar Brands
271: 
272: - **Patagonia** — Same earth-tone editorial identity with full-bleed nature photography and warm cream canvas; both use a single brand color to anchor the page rhythm
273: - **Stripe** — Similar generous pill-button radius and clean white/card layering, though Arva swaps the cool grays for warm cream and introduces a serif voice
274: - **Aesop** — Editorial serif + sans pairing, warm off-white canvas, muted restrained palette, photography that does the heavy visual lifting
275: - **Mailchimp** — Playful oversized pill buttons and a single saturated brand color, though Arva replaces the cartoon illustration system with pastoral landscape photography
276: - **Wren (offset.earth)** — Same regenerative-agriculture visual language: deep forest green brand, cream canvas, full-bleed field photography, and warm pastel content surfaces

Parallax layers (profundidade com translateZ)\ngsap.to(layer1, { y: -100, scrollTrigger: { scrub: true } })\ngsap.to(layer2, { y: -200, scrollTrigger: { scrub: true } })\n\n// 4. Progress indicator\ngsap.to(progressBar, { scaleX: 1, scrollTrigger: { trigger: body, start: 'top top', end: 'bottom bottom', scrub: true } })\n\n// 5. The user wants to add particles / animated background. Let me think about the best approach for this.

For a particle background, I have a few options:
1. **Canvas-based particles** - Custom implementation with requestAnimationFrame
2. **CSS gradient animation** - Simpler, but less "wow"
3. **tsParticles** library - Full-featured but adds bundle size (~50KB)
4. **Custom lightweight canvas** - Party Town style, minimal bundle impact

Since GSAP is already installed and the user wants "wow factor", I'll create a lightweight custom canvas-based particle system that:
- Renders in the hero section background
- Slow-moving particles (like dust motes or stars)
- Reacts to scroll speed via GSAP
- Minimal bundle impact (no extra library)

## Assistant (Build · DeepSeek V4 Flash Free · 26.7s)

_Thinking:_

Now let me create the ParticleBackground component and then integrate it into the LandingPage.

**Tool: write**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "filePath": "C:\\Users\\The Maurá\\Documents\\Projetos\\onibus-kids-tracker-main\\src\\components\\landing\\ParticleBackground.tsx",
  "content": "import { useRef, useEffect } from 'react';\n\ninterface Particle {\n  x: number; y: number; vx: number; vy: number;\n  size: number; alpha: number; alphaSpeed: number;\n  color: string;\n}\n\nconst COLORS = ['rgba(255,255,255,', 'rgba(251,191,36,'];\nconst PARTICLE_COUNT = 50;\n\nconst ParticleBackground: React.FC = () => {\n  const canvasRef = useRef<HTMLCanvasElement>(null);\n  const mouseRef = useRef({ x: -1000, y: -1000 });\n  const rafRef = useRef<number>(0);\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    const canvas = canvasRef.current;\n    if (!canvas) return;\n    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');\n    if (!ctx) return;\n\n    let w = 0, h = 0;\n    const particles: Particle[] = [];\n    let scrollY = 0;\n\n    const resize = () => {\n      w = canvas!.width = window.innerWidth;\n      h = canvas!.height = window.innerHeight;\n    };\n\n    const initParticles = () => {\n      particles.length = 0;\n      for (let i = 0; i < PARTICLE_COUNT; i++) {\n        particles.push({\n          x: Math.random() * w,\n          y: Math.random() * h,\n          vx: (Math.random() - 0.5) * 0.3,\n          vy: (Math.random() - 0.5) * 0.3 - 0.08,\n          size: Math.random() * 2.5 + 1,\n          alpha: Math.random() * 0.5 + 0.15,\n          alphaSpeed: (Math.random() - 0.5) * 0.004,\n          color: COLORS[Math.floor(Math.random() * COLORS.length)],\n        });\n      }\n    };\n\n    const handleScroll = () => {\n      scrollY = window.scrollY;\n    };\n\n    const handleMouse = (e: MouseEvent) => {\n      mouseRef.current.x = e.clientX;\n      mouseRef.current.y = e.clientY;\n    };\n\n    resize();\n    initParticles();\n    window.addEventListener('resize', resize);\n    window.addEventListener('scroll', handleScroll, { passive: true });\n    window.addEventListener('mousemove', handleMouse, { passive: true });\n\n    const draw = () => {\n      ctx!.clearRect(0, 0, w, h);\n      const parallaxOffset = scrollY * 0.15;\n\n      for (const p of particles) {\n        p.x += p.vx;\n        p.y += p.vy;\n        p.alpha += p.alphaSpeed;\n        if (p.alpha > 0.7 || p.alpha < 0.08) p.alphaSpeed *= -1;\n\n        if (p.x < -10) p.x = w + 10;\n        if (p.x > w + 10) p.x = -10;\n        if (p.y < -10) p.y = h + 10;\n        if (p.y > h + 10) p.y = -10;\n\n        const dy = mouseRef.current.y - (p.y + parallaxOffset);\n        const dx = mouseRef.current.x - p.x;\n        const dist = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);\n        if (dist < 150) {\n          p.x -= dx * 0.002;\n          p.y -= dy * 0.002;\n        }\n\n        ctx!.beginPath();\n        ctx!.arc(p.x, p.y + parallaxOffset, p.size, 0, Math.PI * 2);\n        ctx!.fillStyle = p.color + p.alpha + ')';\n        ctx!.fill();\n      }\n\n      rafRef.current = requestAnimationFrame(draw);\n    };\n\n    rafRef.current = requestAnimationFrame(draw);\n\n    return () => {\n      cancelAnimationFrame(rafRef.current);\n      window.removeEventListener('resize', resize);\n      window.removeEventListener('scroll', handleScroll);\n      window.removeEventListener('mousemove', handleMouse);\n    };\n  }, []);\n\n  return (\n    <canvas\n      ref={canvasRef}\n      className=\"absolute inset-0 pointer-events-none z-[1]\"\n      aria-hidden=\"true\"\n    />\n  );\n};\n\nexport default ParticleBackground;\n"
}
```

Wrote file successfully.

<path>C:\Users\The Maurá\Documents\Projetos\onibus-kids-tracker-main\scroll implementacao.txt</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: Build a $5k scroll animation with zero code
2: Hey, it's Cindy 🤍 This is how to build a $5k scroll animation (the Apple product-page effect) with zero code, using AI from start to finish.
3: You know those scroll animations on Apple's product pages, where you scroll down and the product spins, builds itself, or comes apart frame by frame? Agencies charge thousands to build those, because the usual way involves a 3D artist rendering a long image sequence and a developer wiring it to your scroll. It looks expensive because normally it is.
4: 
5: Here is the shortcut. You generate the start and end of the animation with AI, let AI fill in every frame in between, slice that clip into images, and then hand the whole folder to an AI coding tool that wires it to your scroll for you. Four steps, zero code, and the output is the exact technique Apple uses on the AirPods page. Below is the full walkthrough, the build prompt, and three bonus prompts to push it further.
6: 
7: What you're actually building 🧠
8: A scroll-linked image sequence. Instead of a video that plays on its own, you have a stack of still frames painted onto a canvas, and the scroll position decides which frame shows. Scroll down, it steps forward. Scroll up, it steps back. That is why it feels like you are physically controlling the animation, and it is the same trick behind those high-end product pages.
9: 
10: The four steps 🛠

```typescript
const progressRef = useRef(0);

useEffect(() => {
  ScrollTrigger.create({
    trigger: pageRef.current,
    start: 'top top',
    end: 'bottom bottom',
    scrub: 1.5,
    onUpdate: (self) => {
      progressRef.current = self.progress;
      updateBusPosition(self.progress);
    },
  });
}, []);
```

And `updateBusPosition` would map the progress through waypoints:

```typescript
const waypoints = [
  { scrollPos: 0.00, busPos: 0.00 },  // Hero → bus at 0%
  { scrollPos: 0.15, busPos: 0.25 },  // Arrive at Features (25%)
  { scrollPos: 0.25, busPos: 0.25 },  // Pause at Features
  { scrollPos: 0.40, busPos: 0.50 },  // Arrive at Benefits (50%)
  { scrollPos: 0.50, busPos: 0.50 },  // Pause at Benefits
  { scrollPos: 0.65, busPos: 0.75 },  // Arrive at How It Works (75%)

### Architecture

### BusJourney.tsx

```tsx
import React from 'react';
import { Bus } from 'lucide-react';

interface Stop {
  label: string;
  busPct: number;
}

interface BusJourneyProps {
  progress: number;
  activeStop: number;
  stops: Stop[];
}

const BusJourney: React.FC<BusJourneyProps> = ({ progress, activeStop, stops }) => {
  // bus position based on progress
  const busLeft = `${progress}%`;
  
  return (
    <div className="fixed bottom-0 left-0 right-0 z-50 h-[60px] bg-safebus-blue/90 backdrop-blur-sm border-t border-white/10">
      {/* Track */}
      <div className="relative w-full h-full flex items-center">
        {/* Road line */}
        <div className="absolute left-[5%] right-[5%] h-[2px] border-t-2 border-dashed border-white/20" />
        
        {/* Stop markers */}
        {stops.map((stop, i) => (
          <div
            key={i}
            className="absolute -translate-x-1/2 flex flex-col items-center"
            style={{ left: `${stop.busPct}%` }}
          >
            <div className={`w-3 h-3 rounded-full transition-all duration-500 ${
              i <= activeStop ? 'bg-safebus-yellow' : 'bg-white/20'
            }`} />
          </div>
        ))}
        
        {/* Bus */}
        <div
          className="absolute -translate-x-1/2 transition-all duration-300 ease-out"
          style={{ left: `${busLeft}%` }}
        >
          <div className="transform -translate-y-[30px]">
            <div className="w-[44px] h-[28px] bg-safebus-yellow rounded-[4px] relative">
              <div className="absolute top-[4px] left-[6px] right-[6px] h-[10px] flex gap-[3px]">
                <div className="flex-1 bg-safebus-blue rounded-[1px]" />
                <div className="flex-1 bg-safebus-blue rounded-[1px]" />
                <div className="flex-1 bg-safebus-blue rounded-[1px]" />
              </div>
              <div className="absolute -bottom-[5px] left-[6px] w-[8px] h-[8px] rounded-full bg-charcoal" />
              <div className="absolute -bottom-[5px] right-[6px] w-[8px] h-[8px] rounded-full bg-charcoal" />
            </div>
          </div>
        </div>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
};
```

```typescript
const SEGMENTS = [
  // { startScroll, endScroll, startBus, endBus }
  { startScroll: 0.00, endScroll: 0.12, startBus: 0.00, endBus: 0.20 },   // Hero → Features (move)
  { startScroll: 0.12, endScroll: 0.22, startBus: 0.20, endBus: 0.20 },   // Pause at Features

  { startScroll: 0.48, endScroll: 0.60, startBus: 0.45, endBus: 0.70 },   // Benefits → How (move)
  { startScroll: 0.60, endScroll: 0.72, startBus: 0.70, endBus: 0.70 },   // Pause at How
  { startScroll: 0.72, endScroll: 0.85, startBus: 0.70, endBus: 0.90 },   // How → CTA (move)
  { startScroll: 0.85, endScroll: 1.00, startBus: 0.90, endBus: 0.90 },   // Pause at CTA/End
];

     </div>\n    )}\n  </div>\n);\n\nconst BusJourney: React.FC<BusJourneyProps> = ({ progress, activeWaypoint }) => {\n  const moving = SEGMENTS.some(\n    (s) => progress >= s.startScroll && progress < s.endScroll && s.startBus !== s.endBus\n  );\n\n  const ROUTE_PADDING = 8;\n\n  return (\n    <>\n      {/* Road strip behind track */}\n      <div className=\"fixed bottom-0 left-0 right-0 z-50 h-[28px] bg-safebus-blue/95 backdrop-blur-sm border-t border-white/8\">\n        {/* road surface */}\n        <div className=\"absolute inset-0 flex items-center\">\n          {/* dashed center line */}\n          <div\n            className=\"absolute h-[1.5px]\"\n            style={{\n              left: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`,\n              right: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`,\n          <div\n            className=\"absolute h-[1px] bg-white/5\"\n            style={{ left: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`, right: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`, top: '4px' }}\n          />\n          {/* bottom edge */}\n          <div\n            className=\"absolute h-[1px] bg-white/5\"\n            style={{ left: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`, right: `${ROUTE_PADDING}%`, bottom: '4px' }}\n          />\n 'w-[7px] h-[7px] bg-safebus-yellow shadow-[0_0_6px_rgba(251,191,36,0.5)]'\n                    : isActive\n                      ? 'w-[5px] h-[5px] bg-safebus-yellow/60'\n                      : 'w-[4px] h-[4px] bg-white/15'\n                }`}\n              />\n            </div>\n          );\n        })}\n\n        {/* bus */}\n        <div\n          className=\"absolute bottom-0 transition-all duration-[400ms] ease-out\"\n          style={{\n            left: `${ROUTE_PADDING + (progress / 100) * (100 - ROUTE_PADDING * 2)}%`,\n            transform: 'translateX(-50%)',\n          }}\n        >\n          <div className=\"relative\" style={{ bottom: '-2px' }}>\n            <SchoolBusSVG moving={moving} />\n          </div>\n        </div>\n\n        {/* active waypoint label */}\n        {activeWaypoint > 0 && (\n          <div\n            className=\"absolute -top-5 text-[9px] font-medium text-safebus-yellow/70 whitespace-nowrap transition-all duration-500\"\n            style={{\n              left: `${ROUTE_PADDING + (WAYPOINTS[activeWaypoint]?.busPct / 100) * (100 - ROUTE_PADDING * 2)}%`,\n              transform: 'translateX(-50%)',\n              opacity: activeWaypoint > 0 ? 1 : 0,\n            }}\n          >\n            {WAYPOINTS[activeWaypoint]?.label}\n          </div>\n        )}\n      </div>\n\n      {/* spacer so content isn't hidden behind track */}\n      <div className=\"h-[28px]\" />\n    </>\n  );\n};\n\nexport default BusJourney;\n"
}

Let me restructure the approach:

```typescript
const busProgressRef = useRef(0); // for smooth animation
const [activeStop, setActiveStop] = useState(0);

useEffect(() => {
  const page = pageRef.current;
  if (!page) return;
  
  ScrollTrigger.create({
    trigger: page,
    start: 'top top',
    end: 'bottom bottom',
    scrub: 1,
    onUpdate: (self) => {
      const progress = self.progress;
      busProgressRef.current = progress;
      
      // Direct DOM manipulation for bus position
      const busEl = document.querySelector('[data-bus-track]');
      // ... update position
      
      // React state only for waypoint label
      const wp = getActiveWaypoint(progress);
      setActiveStop(prev => prev !== wp ? wp : prev);
    },
  });
}, []);
```

Actually, the BusJourney component receives `progress` as a prop. If I update progress via state on every scroll frame, React will re-render on every frame. That's expensive.

Better approach: Use a ref for the bus position and update the DOM directly. Only update React state for the active waypoint label (which changes infrequently).

Let me refactor BusJourney to support a direct DOM update approach. Or I can use `useState` with the active waypoint and pass a `busRef` for direct positioning.

Actually, let me simplify. I'll use `useState` for the progress but throttle it. Wait, no. Let me think again.

The simplest approach that works well: Use `useState` for both progress and activeWaypoint. React's batching should handle it, and since we're using `requestAnimationFrame` via ScrollTrigger's scrub, it should be smooth enough.

Actually, with React 18's automatic batching and a simple re-render (just updating a number), this should be fine. The DOM changes are minimal (just the bus's `left` style and a few class names).

- Bus at 90% progress: `8 + 90/100 * 84 = 83.6%` (near right)

That looks right! The bus starts at 8% and ends at ~84% of the viewport width.

Let me create the component:

```tsx
const FrameSequence: React.FC<{
  frameCount: number;
  frameDir: string;
  onProgress?: (progress: number) => void;
}> = ({ frameCount, frameDir }) => {
  const containerRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
  const imgRef = useRef<HTMLImageElement>(null);
  const [loaded, setLoaded] = useState(false);
  const [loadProgress, setLoadProgress] = useState(0);
  const currentFrameRef = useRef(0);
  
  // Preload all frames
  useEffect(() => {
    let loaded = 0;
    const total = frameCount;
    const images: HTMLImageElement[] = [];
    
    for (let i = 1; i <= total; i++) {
      const img = new Image();
      img.onload = () => {
        loaded++;
        setLoadProgress(loaded / total);
        if (loaded === total) setLoaded(true);
      };
      img.onerror = () => {
        loaded++;
        if (loaded === total) setLoaded(true);
      };
      img.src = `${frameDir}/image_${String(i).padStart(2, '0')}.jpg`;
      images.push(img);
    }
    
    return () => images.forEach(img => { img.onload = null; img.onerror = null; });
  }, [frameCount, frameDir]);
  
  // GSAP ScrollTrigger
  useEffect(() => {
    if (!containerRef.current || !imgRef.current) return;
    
    const ctx = gsap.context(() => {
      ScrollTrigger.create({
        trigger: containerRef.current,
        start: 'top top',
        end: 'bottom top',
        pin: true,
        scrub: 1,
        onUpdate: (self) => {
          const frame = Math.max(1, Math.min(frameCount, Math.round(self.progress * (frameCount - 1)) + 1));
          if (frame !== currentFrameRef.current) {
            currentFrameRef.current = frame;
            const src = `${frameDir}/image_${String(frame).padStart(2, '0')}.jpg`;
            if (imgRef.current) imgRef.current.src = src;
          }
        },
      });
    });
    
    return () => ctx.revert();
  }, [frameCount, frameDir, loaded]);
  
  return (
    <div ref={containerRef}>
      {!loaded && <div>Loading... {Math.round(loadProgress * 100)}%</div>}
      <img ref={imgRef} src={`${frameDir}/image_01.jpg`} />
    </div>
  );
};
```

But you know what, the cleanest approach for a frame sequence is actually to use a stacking context with all images layered on top of each other, and only the current frame visible:

```tsx
{Array.from({length: 20}, (_, i) => (
  <img
    key={i}
    src={`/frames/image_${String(i + 1).padStart(2, '0')}.jpg`}
    className={`absolute inset-0 w-full h-full object-cover transition-opacity duration-0 ${currentFrame === i + 1 ? 'opacity-100' : 'opacity-0'}`}
  />
))}
```

But this renders 20 img tags. That's OK for 20 images.

Actually, the most efficient way is:
1. Preload all images into an array
2. Use a single canvas element
3. On scroll update, draw the preloaded image onto the canvas

Let me go with a canvas approach. It's the "pro" way to do it.

```tsx
const ScrollFrameSequence: React.FC = () => {
  const containerRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);
  const canvasRef = useRef<HTMLCanvasElement>(null);
  const [loaded, setLoaded] = useState(false);
  const [loadPct, setLoadPct] = useState(0);
  const imagesRef = useRef<HTMLImageElement[]>([]);
  
  useEffect(() => {
    const total = TOTAL_FRAMES;
    const imgs: HTMLImageElement[] = [];
    let loadedCount = 0;
    
    for (let i = 1; i <= total; i++) {
      const img = new Image();
      img.onload = () => {
        loadedCount++;
        setLoadPct(loadedCount / total);
        if (loadedCount === total) setLoaded(true);
      };
      img.src = `${FRAMES_PATH}${String(i).padStart(2, '0')}.jpg`;
      imgs.push(img);
    }
    imagesRef.current = imgs;
    
    return () => {
      imgs.forEach(img => { img.onload = null; });
    };
  }, []);
  
  useEffect(() => {
    if (!canvasRef.current || !loaded) return;
    
    const canvas = canvasRef.current;
    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');
    if (!ctx) return;
    
    const resize = () => {
      canvas.width = window.innerWidth;
      canvas.height = window.innerHeight;
      // Draw first frame
      drawFrame(1, ctx);
    };
    
    const drawFrame = (frame: number, context: CanvasRenderingContext2D) => {
      const img = imagesRef.current[frame - 1];
      if (!img) return;
      const w = canvas.width;
      const h = canvas.height;
      const iw = img.naturalWidth;
      const ih = img.naturalHeight;
      const scale = Math.max(w / iw, h / ih);
      const sw = iw * scale;
      const sh = ih * scale;
      const sx = (w - sw) / 2;
      const sy = (h - sh) / 2;
      context.drawImage(img, sx, sy, sw, sh);
    };
    
    resize();
    window.addEventListener('resize', resize);
    
    // GSAP
    const ctx_gsap = gsap.context(() => {
      if (!containerRef.current) return;
      ScrollTrigger.create({
        trigger: containerRef.current,
        start: 'top top',
        end: 'bottom top',
        pin: true,
        scrub: 1,
        onUpdate: (self) => {
          const frame = Math.max(1, Math.min(TOTAL_FRAMES, Math.round(self.progress * (TOTAL_FRAMES - 1) + 1)));
          drawFrame(frame, ctx);
        },
      });
    });
    
    return () => {
      ctx_gsap.revert();
      window.removeEventListener('resize', resize);
    };
  }, [loaded]);
  
  return (
    <div ref={containerRef} className="relative w-full h-screen">
      {!loaded && <div>Loading frames...</div>}
      <canvas ref={canvasRef} className="w-full h-full object-cover" />
    </div>
  );
};
```

This is clean. Let me now write the full component and integrate it.

But wait, I need to think about how this integrates with the existing hero. Currently the hero has:
- Background image + gradient overlay
- ParticleBackground
- Navbar (absolute top)
- Content (badge, title, text, buttons, social proof)
- Scroll indicator

The frame sequence should replace the background image. The gradient overlay and particle background should remain on top. The content should remain as-is but could fade out as the frames progress.

Let me replace the heroBgRef div (which has the static image) with the frame sequence canvas. The gradient overlay goes on top of the canvas. Particles go on top. Content stays on top.

The tricky part: the heroBgRef was previously a div with background-image. Now it needs to be the frame sequence container + canvas + gradient overlay.

And for the bus journey, only the post-hero sections are tracked.

```typescript
ScrollTrigger.create({
  trigger: statsRef.current,
  start: 'top bottom',
  end: 'bottom bottom',
  scrub: 1,
  onUpdate: (self) => {
    const raw = self.progress;
    const mapped = mapScrollToBus(raw);
    setBusProgress(mapped);
    const wp = getActiveWaypoint(raw);
    if (wp !== lastWpRef.current) {
      lastWpRef.current = wp;

});
```

const POST_HERO_SEGMENTS = [
  { startScroll: 0.00, endScroll: 0.15, startBus: 0.00, endBus: 20.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.15, endScroll: 0.28, startBus: 20.00, endBus: 20.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.28, endScroll: 0.42, startBus: 20.00, endBus: 45.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.42, endScroll: 0.55, startBus: 45.00, endBus: 45.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.55, endScroll: 0.68, startBus: 45.00, endBus: 70.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.68, endScroll: 0.80, startBus: 70.00, endBus: 70.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.80, endScroll: 0.92, startBus: 70.00, endBus: 90.00 },
  { startScroll: 0.92, endScroll: 1.00, startBus: 90.00, endBus: 90.00 },
];
```

{

  "content": "import { useRef, useEffect, useState } from 'react';\nimport gsap from 'gsap';\nimport { ScrollTrigger } from 'gsap/ScrollTrigger';\n\ngsap.registerPlugin(ScrollTrigger);\n\nconst TOTAL_FRAMES = 20;\nconst FRAME_PATH = '/frames/image_';\n\ninterface Props {\n  onProgress?: (pct: number) => void;\n}\n\nfunction pad(n: number) {\n  return String(n).padStart(2, '0');\n}\n\nconst ScrollFrameSequence: React.FC<Props> = ({ onProgress }) => {\n  const sectionRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null);\n  const canvasRef = useRef<HTMLCanvasElement>(null);\n  const [loaded, setLoaded] = useState(false);\n  const [loadPct, setLoadPct] = useState(0);\n\n  const framesRef = useRef<HTMLImageElement[]>([]);\n  const currentRef = useRef(0);\n\n  /* preload all frames */\n  useEffect(() => {\n    let done = 0;\n    const imgs: HTMLImageElement[] = [];\n\n    for (let i = 1; i <= TOTAL_FRAMES; i++) {\n      const img = new Image();\n      img.onload = () => {\n        done++;\n        setLoadPct(done / TOTAL_FRAMES);\n        if (done === TOTAL_FRAMES) setLoaded(true);\n      };\n      img.onerror = () => {\n        done++;\n        if (done === TOTAL_FRAMES) setLoaded(true);\n      };\n      img.src = `${FRAME_PATH}${pad(i)}.jpg`;\n      imgs.push(img);\n    }\n\n    framesRef.current = imgs;\n    return () => {\n      imgs.forEach((img) => { img.onload = null; img.onerror =   if (!canvas) return;\n    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');\n    if (!ctx) return;\n\n    const resize = () => {\n      const dpr = window.devicePixelRatio || 1;\n      canvas.width = window.innerWidth * dpr;\n      canvas.height = window.innerHeight * dpr;\n      canvas.style.width = `${window.innerWidth}px`;\n      canvas.style.height = `${window.innerHeight}px`;\n 58:     if (!canvas) return;
59:     const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');

{
  "filePath": "C:\\Users\\The Maurá\\Documents\\Projetos\\onibus-kids-tracker-main\\src\\components\\landing\\ScrollFrameSequence.tsx",
  "content": "import { useRef, useEffect, useState, useCallback } from 'react';\n\nconst TOTAL_FRAMES = 20;\nconst FRAME_PATH = '/frames/image_';\n\nfunction pad(n: number) {\n  return String(n).padStart(2, '0');\n}\n\ninterface Props {\n  /** Exposed so parent can call draw(frameNum) directly */\n  drawRef?: React.MutableRefObject<((frame: number) => void) | null>;\n}\n\nconst ScrollFrameSequence: React.FC<Props> = ({ drawRef }) => {\n  const canvasRef = useRef<HTMLCanvasElement>(null);\n  const [loaded, setLoaded] = useState(false);\n  const [loadPct, setLoadPct] = useState(0);\n  const imagesRef = useRef<HTMLImageElement[]>([]);\n  const ctxRef = useRef<CanvasRenderingContext2D | null>(null);\n\n  /* preload all frames into memory */\n  useEffect(() => {\n    let done = 0;\n    const imgs: HTMLImageElement[] = [];\n    for (let i = 1; i <= TOTAL_FRAMES; i++) {\n      const img = new Image();\n      img.onload = () => {\n        done++;\n        setLoadPct(done / TOTAL_FRAMES);\n        if (done === TOTAL_FRAMES) setLoaded(true);\n      };\n      img.onerror = () => {\n        done++;\n        if (done === TOTAL_FRAMES) setLoaded(true);\n      };\n      img.src = `${FRAME_PATH}${pad(i)}.jpg`;\n      imgs.push(img);\n    }\n    imagesRef.current = imgs;\n    return () => {\n      imgs.forEach((img) => { img.onload = null; img.onerror = null; });\n    };\n  }, []);\n\n  /* initialise canvas + resize */\n  useEffect(() => {\n    const canvas = canvasRef.current;\n    if (!canvas) return;\n    const ctx = canvas.getContext('2d');\n    if (!ctx) return;\n    ctxRef.current = ctx;\n\n    function resize() {\n      const dpr = window.devicePixelRatio || 1;\n      canvas!.width = window.innerWidth * dpr;\n      canvas!.height = window.innerHeight * dpr;\n      canvas!.style.width = `${window.innerWidth}px`;\n      canvas!.style.height = `${window.innerHeight}px`;\n    }\n\n    resize();\n    window.addEventListener('resize', resize);\n    return () => window.removeEventListener('resize', resize);\n  }, []);\n\n  /* draw a specific frame — reset transform each time because canvas context resets on resize */\n  const draw = useCallback((frame: number) => {\n    const img = imagesRef.current[frame - 1];\n    if (!img || !img.complete) return;\n    const canvas = canvasRef.current;\n    if (!canvas) return;\n    const ctx = ctxRef.current;\n    if (!ctx) return;\n\n    const dpr = window.devicePixelRatio || 1;\n    const w = window.innerWidth;\n    const h = window.innerHeight;\n\n    /* reset transform and clear */\n    ctx.setTransform(dpr, 0, 0, dpr, 0, 0);\n    ctx.clearRect(0, 0, w, h);\n\n    const iw = img.naturalWidth || 1920;\n    const ih = img.naturalHeight || 1080;\n    const scale = Math.max(w / iw, h / ih);\n    const sw = iw * scale;\n    const sh = ih * scale;\n    const sx = (w - sw) / 2;\n    const sy = (h - sh) / 2;\n    ctx.drawImage(img, sx, sy, sw, sh);\n  }, []);\n\n  /* draw first frame once loaded */\n  useEffect(() => {\n    if (!loaded) return;\n    draw(1);\n  }, [loaded, draw]);\n\n  /* expose draw to parent */\n  useEffect(() => {\n    if (drawRef) {\n      drawRef.current = draw;\n    }\n  }, [draw, drawRef]);\n\n  return (\n    <>\n      {!loaded && (\n        <div className=\"absolute inset-0 z-30 flex flex-col items-center justify-center bg-safebus-blue\">\n          <div className=\"w-10 h-10 border-2 border-white/20 border-t-safebus-yellow rounded-full animate-spin mb-4\" />\n          <p className=\"text-white/60 text-[13px] font-medium tracking-[0.025em]\">\n            A preparar experiência... {Math.round(loadPct * 100)}%\n          </p>\n        </div>\n      )}\n      <canvas\n        ref={canvasRef}\n        className=\"absolute inset-0 w-full h-full\"\n        aria-hidden=\"true\"\n      />\n    </>\n  );\n};\n\nexport default ScrollFrameSequence;\n"
}
